alt="Steve Jobs&#39; letter to Apple board and community" title="">Article: Steve Jobs' letter to Apple board and community</a><p><em>AP - 53 mins ago</em></p></li><li class="story collapsed"><span href="/10-products-defined-steve-jobs-career-000908909.html;_ylt=Arhgoy_wSxzfS2CkkK225Lw6cOF_;_ylu=X3oDMTNrcjAyc25wBHBrZwNkMDBmNjg5NC1iMDA4LTMzNGQtYWIwMy00YzFhODBmNTgyNDEEcG9zAzMEc2VjA01lZGlhQXJ0aWNsZUJvZHlBc3NlbWJseQR2ZXIDZTNiYjZlYzAtY2ViYy0xMWUwLTljZGYtYzg2OWJjNzU2ZmE3;_ylg=X3oDMTM2MDF2ZWxiBGludGwDdXMEbGFuZwNlbi11cwRwc3RhaWQDN2YyNTIzMGMtODhkNy0zNWVmLTllY2YtYTk1NTczODgxYTkxBHBzdGNhdAN0ZWNofHdpcmVsZXNzBHB0A3N0b3J5cGFnZQR0ZXN0Aw--;_ylv=3" alt="10 products that defined Steve Jobs&#39; career" title="">Article: 10 products that defined Steve Jobs' career</a><p><em>AP - 55 mins ago</em></p></li><li class="story collapsed"><span class="icon-container icon-story"></span><a href="/chronology-steve-jobs-apple-004724177.html;_ylt=AuKjdDte3BjU7I9yzcvorvo6cOF_;_ylu=X3oDMTNraGlrcm83BHBrZwNjMzVkYmMwMy05YTQ3LTNjNzQtOGM2MC1kNmY5ODgzN2FkYjgEcG9zAzQEc2VjA01lZGlhQXJ0aWNsZUJvZHlBc3NlbWJseQR2ZXIDZTg5YzVkNTAtY2ViYy0xMWUwLWJkM2ItMjRlYWJlYjc4OTk1;_ylg=X3oDMTM2MDF2ZWxiBGludGwDdXMEbGFuZwNlbi11cwRwc3RhaWQDN2YyNTIzMGMtODhkNy0zNWVmLTllY2YtYTk1NTczODgxYTkxBHBzdGNhdAN0ZWNofHdpcmVsZXNzBHB0A3N0b3J5cGFnZQR0ZXN0Aw--;_ylv=3" alt="A chronology of Steve Jobs at Apple" title="">Article: A chronology of Steve Jobs at Apple</a><p><em>AP - 57 mins ago</em></p></li><li class="story collapsed last"><span class="icon-container icon-story"></span><a href="/biographical-information-apple-ceo-cook-011542337.html" alt="Biographical information on new Apple CEO Cook" title="">Article: Biographical information on new Apple CEO Cook</a><p><em>AP - 39 mins ago</em></p></li></ul></div></div></div>SAN FRANCISCO (AP) — Steve Jobs, the mind behind the iPhone, iPad and other devices that turned Apple Inc. into one of the world&#39;s most powerful companies, resigned as CEO on Wednesday, saying he can no longer handle the job but will continue to play a leadership role.</p><p>The move appears to be the result of an unspecified medical condition for which Jobs took a leave from his post in January. Apple&#39;s chief operating officer, Tim Cook, was quickly named CEO of the company Jobs co-founded 35 years ago in his garage.</p><p>In a letter addressed to Apple&#39;s board and the &quot;Apple community,&quot; Jobs said he &quot;always said if there ever came a day when I could no longer meet my duties and expectations as Apple&#39;s CEO, I would be the first to let you know. Unfortunately, that day has come.&quot;</p><p>The company said Jobs gave the board his resignation Wednesday and suggested Cook be named the company&#39;s new leader. Apple said Jobs was elected board chairman and Cook is becoming a member of its board.</p><p>Genentech Inc. Chairman Art Levinson, in a statement issued on behalf of Apple&#39;s board, said Jobs&#39; &quot;extraordinary vision and leadership saved Apple and guided it to its position as the world&#39;s most innovative and valuable technology company.&quot;</p><p>He said that Jobs will continue to provide &quot;his unique insights, creativity and inspiration,&quot; and that the board has &quot;complete confidence&quot; that Cook is the right person to replace him.</p><p>&quot;&quot;Tim&#39;s 13 years of service to Apple have been marked by outstanding performance, and he has demonstrated remarkable talent and sound judgment in everything he does,&quot; Levinson said.</p><p>Jobs&#39; health has long been a concern for Apple investors who see him as an industry oracle who seems to know what consumers want long before they do. After his announcement, Apple stock quickly fell 5.4 percent in after-hours trading.</p><p>Jeff Gamet, managing editor of The Mac Observer online news site focused on Apple, said Jobs&#39; departure has more sentimental than practical significance, and that he has been telegraphing the change for several years.</p><p>&quot;All Apple really has done is made official what they&#39;ve been doing administratively for a while now, which is Tim runs the show and Steve gets to do his part to make sure the products come out to meet the Apple standard,&quot; he said.</p><p>&quot;I expect that even though there are a lot of people that right now are sad or scared because Steve is stepping back from the CEO role, that ultimately they&#39;ll be OK,&quot; Gamet said.</p><p>But Trip Chowdhry, an analyst with Global Equities Research, said Jobs&#39; maniacal attention to detail is what set Apple apart. He said Apple&#39;s product pipeline might be secure for another few years, but predicted that the company will eventually struggle to come up with market-changing ideas.</p><p>&quot;Apple is Steve Jobs, Steve Jobs is Apple, and Steve Jobs is innovation,&quot; Chowdhry said. &quot;You can teach people how to be operationally efficient, you can hire consultants to tell you how to do that, but God creates innovation. ... Apple without Steve Jobs is nothing.&quot;</p><p><div class="yog-col yog-16u" style="float:left"><div class="yom-mod yom-iframe" id="mediaiframe"><div class="bd"><div class="yom-iframe-wrap" id="mediaiframe-ifr" style="width:100%;height:560px;"><noscript><iframe src="http://hosted.ap.org/interactives/2011/steve-jobs-apple/content.swf?SITE" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" style="width:100%;height:560px;"> </iframe></noscript></div></div></div></div></p><p>Earlier this month Apple became the most valuable company in America, briefly surpassing Exxon Mobil. At the market close Wednesday its market value was $349 billion, just behind Exxon Mobil&#39;s $358 billion.</p><p>Jobs&#39; hits seemed to grow bigger as the years went on: After the colorful iMac computer and the now-ubiquitous iPod, the iPhone redefined the category of smart phones and the iPad all but created the market for tablet computers.</p><p>His own aura seemed part of the attraction. On stage at trade shows and company events in his uniform of jeans, sneakers and black mock-turtlenecks, he&#39;d entrance audiences with new devices, new colors, new software features, building up to a grand finale he&#39;d predictably preface by saying, &quot;One more thing.&quot;</p><p>Jobs, 56, shepherded Apple from a two-man startup to Silicon Valley darling when the Apple II, the first computer for regular people to really catch on, sent IBM Corp. and others scrambling to get their own PCs to market.</p><p>After Apple suffered a slump in the mid-1980s, he was forced out of the company. He was CEO at Next, another computer company, and Pixar, the computer-animation company that produced &quot;Toy Story&quot; on his watch, over the following 10 years.</p><p>Apple was foundering as he returned as an adviser in 1996 — a year it lost $900 million as Microsoft Windows-based PCs dominated the computer market. The company&#39;s fortunes began to turn around with its first new product under Jobs&#39; direction, the iMac, which launched in 1998 and sold about 2 million in its first 12 months.</p><p>Jobs eventually became interim CEO, then took the job permanently. Apple&#39;s popularity grew in the U.S. throughout the 2000s as the ever-sleeker line of iPods introduced many lifelong Windows users to their first Apple gadget. Apple created another sensation in 2007 with the iPhone, the stark-looking but powerful smart phone that quickly dominated the industry.</p><p>The iPad was introduced less than a year and a half ago but has already sold nearly 29 million units as it inspired myriad rivals in a tablet computer market that scarcely existed before Apple stepped in.</p><p>There have been some setbacks. Apple was swept up in a massive Securities and Exchange Commission inquiry into stock options backdating in the mid-2000s, a practice that artificially boosted the value of options grants. But Jobs and Apple emerged unscathed after two former executives took the fall and eventually settled with the SEC.</p><p>As Jobs was praised for his vision, concerns about his health persisted. The January leave was Jobs&#39; third medical leave over several years. He had previously survived pancreatic cancer and received a liver transplant.</p><p>Shannon Cross, an analyst at Cross Research, said Cook is a good choice to replace Jobs.</p><p>&quot;He has taken over for Jobs twice in two medical leaves and the company has functioned extremely well,&quot; she said, adding that Cook has been Jobs&#39; &quot;right hand guy&quot; for many years.</p><p>Cross also said Jobs put in place a &quot;culture of innovation&quot; that will help Apple remain a creative force in the industry.</p><p>&quot;Steve Jobs is an extremely strong leader and clearly has made Apple a leading consumer electronics company and one of the most innovative companies in the world,&quot; she said. &quot;However, he didn&#39;t do it alone.&quot;</p><p>___</p><p>AP Technology Writer Barbara Ortutay in San Francisco contributed to this report.</p></div></div>
